<div class="word-content">
<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;
margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:center'><b><span
style='font-size:14.0pt'>Part I: OVERVIEW OF CHRISTIAN APOLOGETICS </span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;
margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:center'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;
margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:center'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>Virgil Warren, PhD</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;
margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:center'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;
margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:center'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Apologetics, used in a non-technical
sense, deals with three components that unite in the process of coming to faith
and continuing in it. The conviction is that the process of apologetics is the
same as the process of evangelism. Apologetics and evangelism see it from
different viewpoints. Evangelism thinks of it from the viewpoint of the
communicator and sees it as communication; apologetics thinks of it from the
viewpoint of the hearer and sees it as conversion. What is seen and thought
about, however, is the same thing. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:8.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;
margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:center'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'><img width=395 height=219
src="/cir-library/images/essays/part-i-overview-of-christian-apologetics/image001.png"></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>God intends meaning into the event by putting it in
connection with a purpose.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:40.5pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> There are several advantages to this format as the
basis for faith and a framework for presentation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (a)  It helps picture where individuals
are coming from as they interact with the presentation of the gospel. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (b)  It helps keep a balanced diet
of reasons to believe so people do not end up with a deformed faith because of
a deformed reason for having it.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (c)  It gives a more convincing
foundation for a presenters own faith.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (d)  It gives a variety of
approaches so the presenter does not limit himself to a certain type of person that
can respond to a particular canned approach.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Coming to Christian faith begins with (1)
a persons sense of perceived need, which in turn opens him up to (2) the central
defense of Christianity: the death-resurrection of Jesus Christ. The meaning of
the Christ event was intended into that event and arises from within it. When
people begin to live in terms of that meaning, they have (3) a sense of
fulfillment: <i>The proof of the pudding is in the eating.</i> This process
helps refine and redefine perceived needs, bringing them into conformity with
the new perspectives that Christian faith offers.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Besides the patterns clockwise flow,
counterclockwise reciprocation occurs between (3) the experience of Christian
living and (2) the objective Christian faith inasmuch as the involvement in the
faith helps a person appreciate the faith itself. Reciprocation also occurs
between (2) the basis-content and (1) the sense of need because the content of
the good news adjusts perceived needs to real needs. The three points of the
triangle have <u>individual</u>, <u>cumulative</u>, and <u>reciprocal</u>
force.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> The triangular format can serve to present
any <u>religion</u> or philosophy. It outlines what we can call <u>advertising</u>.
It pictures the format of <u>scientific</u> endeavor: isolating a problem,
hypothesizing a solution, experimenting to verify the hypothesis. There is a
difference, though, between philosophical method and scientific method and the
format as applied to the Christian faith. Step 2 does not come from step 1 here
as it does in philosophy and science. Human need does not generate the answer;
it fosters a willingness to hear the answer that comes from another sourcethe historical
events.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>Several elements in the above schematic contrast with
alternatives often proposed.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (1) <u>The kind of certainty</u>. The
certainty implied by Christian evidences is not <u>logical/mathematical
certainty</u> as in the equation 2 x 2 = 4. In a mathematical equation each
number and function are defined so the equation presents a definitional
manipulation. Christian evidence provides for <u>psychological certainty</u>, as
in the conviction that we are awake rather than dreaming or watching a football
game rather than mowing the lawn. It is the kind of certainty we have that our mothers
are their mothers. Christian apologetics occurs (A) in the realm of reality
more than (B)in the realm of idea.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> In the taxonomy of certainty (a
subset of epistemology), there is a difference in the degrees and kinds of
certainty, as noted above. Mathematical certainty is (a) metaphysical
certainty, which differs from (b) real-world certainty. The latter can be
direct, personal experience (sight, as in 2 Corinthians <b>5</b>:7) or
indirect experience (faith) through other people that tell us about things beyond
our experience, before our experience (history), and future to our experience(eschatology).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (2) <u>The reason for faith</u>. The
reason for religious faith is threefold, not singular. Christianity is not (2b)
a philosophy to believe; it is a religion to live (3). It is not (2) a history
to know; it is (1) something needed that we sense.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (3) <u>The beginning of Christian
evidences</u>. Christian evidences begin in the present <u>subjective</u>
viewpoint as far as coming to, and growing in, Christ is concerned. The <u>objective</u>
beginning is the past Christ event that created the content of the faith (see
below under point 5). We believe not only because (3) the Christian faith works
in real life<u>the pragmatic proving</u>; nor even because (2) the event it came
from actually happened<u>the historical proof</u>; but because (1) our need
forces us to believe in something. Practically speaking, something is true to
the extent that it works. Historically something is true whether anybody
believes it or not. Subjectively Christianity can become true, so a reasonable
person should not treat its claims in an academic manner. Before the Christian
message came, there was already reason to believe it. Many of us have not
accepted Christ and may never do so: we have no conscious sense of need for
what the gospel offers. History is the <u>logical beginning point</u>. Need is
the <u>chronological beginning point</u> for each person. Need and experience
are secondary and confirmatory whereas the Christ event is primary.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (4) <u>The manner of relationship between
need, basis, and experience</u>. A manner of relationship between need, basis,
and experience is implied by the beginning point. <u>There is continuity
between elements</u>, which provides movement from one to the next. Beginning
at (1) stands over against beginning at (3) with a leap of faith into the
experience. Such an approach would adopt a conclusion without knowing the basis
for it. Beginning at (3) could mean in effect living, not by principle (2), but
by pleasure. Theoretically people could be coaxed into trying a way of life
that is sinful, harmful, and false before they find out it has those qualities
and effects. Sometimes it is too late then to reverse the consequences. It is
better for Christians to have leaped, of course, because they landed somewhere
good; but the approach to God does not require such a leap since there is
continuity between the position of unbelief and that of belief and commitment. Christian
outreach is not limited to <i>try it, youll like it.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Beginning at (1) also stands over against
another kind of discontinuity: the coming of faith implanted directly by the
Holy Spirit. In this scenario the Spirit works <u>parallel to the word</u> or
any other conditioning factor. He works directly on us, who have no power to
leap. But scripture describes conversion as coming to faith <u>through the word</u>.
The problem in the previous paragraph was the lack of connection by which we
could move to faith. Here the problem is a lack in the us to appreciate the connection
between the historical truth (2a + b) and our need (1). The complexity of
conversion and the real work of the Spirit in it does not make it miraculous or
take away any connection between where we are and where we need to be. The song
does speak correctly, <i>Till by faith I met Him face to face and I felt the
wonder of His graceThen I knew that He was more than just a God who didnt
care . . . ,</i> but that does not tell the whole story.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Beginning at (1) also contrasts with
evangelizing a present person with the recitation of past facts: <i>Sure, He
came to set his people freeWhat is that to me?</i> Relevance is involved
because caring about people must set the atmosphere for witness, and the
ability to be loved is the point of contact for that witness.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> The manner of relationship between the
primary parts has a second aspect: <u>there is reciprocation between parts
rather than only a straight-line series</u>. The schematic moves backwards as
well as forward. That fact explains why the pilgrimage is not the same in every
conversion. It explains why people believe for originally different reasons. It
shows why various approaches can be effective though perhaps with varying
degrees of success and validity. The reciprocal character of needs, basis,
and experience also explains why coming to commitment may take a while instead
of being immediate. Finally, it illustrates why being a Christian is subject to
growth.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> As to different pilgrimages, many believe
because (3) they never disbelieved. They were raised in Christian homes and
began at stage three. In the fellowship of the family, they experienced the
love of Christ fulfilling their need to be loved. The reciprocal connection
meant that later they became increasingly aware of the reason their family lived
that way, which caused them to move from (3) to (2), so their practice took on
a reason for itself.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Others come to faith because (2b) they
have heard the message proclaimed. <i>The</i> [subconscious?] <i>secrets of their
hearts were made manifest</i> (to themselves? 1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:24-25). From
the answer they became aware of the problem, moving from (2b) to (1). Again,
faith may come because (2a) the historical credentials of Christianity have
convinced them. What it claims happened did happen and must have come from a
God (John <b>3</b>:2) <i>who loves me and gave himself for me</i> (Galatians <b>2</b>:20),
who must exist, and so on.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Finally, still others accept Christ
because (1) they have suffered, suffered loss, or experienced a crisis that
swept aside the shackles of academic disbelief, and forced them to gain
perspective and seek someone beyond themselvessomeone who is <i>bigger than
you and I.</i> They move from (1) to (2b) and then to (2a).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> The chronological sequence of the process
does not always correlate with the logical one. All the components must be
there, however, or faith is deformed and may not last. Any believer can and
does contribute something to winning someone else. Some may help one kind of
disbeliever through the decision point; others may help a different kind. The
time element means that the witness to unbelievers must never cease, and that
the believer himself always has somewhere to grow. Understanding the kind of
relationship between (1) and (2) is important. The Christian message does not come
from the need (1) but through history (1a; cp. point 5 below). The connections between
the components are personal, more than metaphysical and logical. They are
personal capacities of mind, emotion, will, communication, exhortation, love,
and the like.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> It might be well to observe at this point
that theologically it is not possible to go from (1) to (3). However, (a) people
can <u>unconsciously</u> pick up a way of acting without realizing <u>that</u> they
are doing it or <u>why</u>. Imitation is a way of learning that does not
involve why people do something a certain way, which can create problems if the
rest of the picture is not get filled in.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (5) <u>The origin of Christian truth</u>. The
idea here has to do with the beginning of truth itself as distinguished from a persons
coming to know it (epistemology; see point 3 above). Coming to know about it
relates to Christian evidences. The origin of Christian truth and meaning lies
in the sovereign God who purposes. The content of the Christian faith is not
kicked up by the hearers need, as indicated in point 4. Schleiermachers
notion of <i>the sense of absolute dependence </i>(<i>Abhngigkeit</i>) is a
stimulating concept, but the father of modern theology made a fundamental
departure when he tried to develop the <u>content</u> of faith out of the <u>need</u>
for it. The fact of dependence does not prove there is something to depend on,
nor does a need create the answer out of itself in a kind of self-creation <i>ex
nihilo</i> (cp. <i>die Religionsgeschichte Schule</i>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Historically Schleiermacher was
reacting in part to another false starting point prevalent in the attempt of
scholastic theology to deduce Christian content from first principles. His,
then, was an attempt to develop religious truth from fundamental human
experience (empiricism, existentialism) rather than deduce them philosophically
from first principles (rationalism). He opted for an empirical starting point
rather than a philosophical one. Both approaches, however, end up confusing
epistemology with truth in correlation with letting the objective dissolve into
the subjective.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The nature of a problem restricts
the possibilities for answering it, but it does not establish a specific
alternative. Furthermore, a person can misperceive the need. Theology from
experience assumes that experience has the character of revelation and that it
has sufficient clarity to produce distinctives of the Christian faith. Experience
does provide a door for the knowledge of God to enter, but experience is
subject to greater ambiguity than propositional revelation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The alternative proposed here is
that God determines meaning, because only an independent (sovereign) being can
purpose without fear of frustration from above. And it is from purpose that action
arisesan action like the Christ event. Therefore, the meaning of the Christ
event is <u>in</u> the event as opposed to being <u>read into</u> it by a
viewer or deduced somehow from an original starting point. Subjectively reading
meaning into the event occurs in theology from below, anthropological
theology, eschatological theology, neo-orthodoxy. Deducing meaning from an
original starting point occurred in scholasticism. But the meaning of an event
is intended into it by its Purposer and actor: <i>the God and father of our
Lord Jesus Christ.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> <u>Truth and meaning</u> are determined in
the manner described. <u>Coming to know</u> that meaning is by propositional
revelation (explanation) if the revelatory event is not sufficiently clear in
itself. For example, Jesus indicated ahead of time the meaning of his
death-resurrection: a ransom for many; <i>that you might have life . . .
abundantly,</i> and so on. Inasmuch as that occurrence involved a miraculous
element, it confirmed that truth claim; so the beholders could <u>rely on what
they came to know</u>. Meaning is determined by the <u>purposer</u>, conveyed
by the purposers <u>proposition</u>, and authenticated by <u>miracle</u>
(Romans <b>1</b>:3).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> The meaning of the Christ event was in the
event because it was intended into it. That contrasts with saying that an event
means what it eventuates into; that it means what it comes to mean. What an
event eventuates into may be connected with it all right as in a series of
cause-effects in nature, but at best this only comes to recognize that meaning.
What an event eventuates into stems from peoples response to it, which rests
on their perceptions. The Christ event did not mean what we see as its effect
on human civilization afterwards. We even venture to say that the meaning of
the Christ event in that sense of futurum was not always even good, much less
true. The incarnation did not mean what it did because of its effect on the
direction of civilization, because such a thing stems from reading meaning into
it. It comes from persons responses to the historical figure Jesus of
Nazareth. What subsequently occurred may tend to <u>show</u> what it meant, but
what it meant was determined by the God who brought it about. As predestination
teaches, meaning is ultimately intended into history from the outside by God
rather than being read into from the inside it by people.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> What happened in the Christ event is not
as crucial as the meaning of what happened. Meaning is revealed by miracle,
prophecy, and the power of a message that correlates with experience and
exhibits internal consistency.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (6) <u>The nature of Christian evidences</u>.
Apologetics is <u>historical</u> because Christianity itself is <u>historically,
rather than philosophically, based. It is unique among world religions in that
respect</u>. Because the message is historically based, the event <u>is</u> the
message and the fact that it happened proves that this truth exists. The
occurrence of a resurrection proves that resurrection can happen. The
historical basis of Christianity means that theology and apologetics both come
through historical eventthe same historical event. Christs life-death-resurrection
forms a fact-meaning composite that by being miraculous also proves it is true.
By declaration his death means redemption from death and is proved to have that
meaning by resurrection. Because Christianity deals with people in history, it
is historical, and its evidences are historical. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Implied in the schematic is that Christian
apologetics as history is holistic. It speaks to both the <u>affective</u> and <u>cognitive</u>
aspects of the human person. In this way, it is amenable to the ones that Christian
evidence addresses. The objective basis (2a + b) addresses the cognitive side
while the subjective part (1 + 3) addresses the affective side. In short, love
is both contentful and motivational because it bonds social relationships. The
Christian message centers on love (2b), was established because of love (2a),
is transmitted through the medium of love (3), and answers the need to be loved
(1).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Christian evidence combines faith and
sight. It is sight in stations (1) and (3); it is faith in station (2) because
for us the non-recurring events that establish the foundations for the faith
are not directly accessible. Faith contrasts with sight (2 Corinthians <b>5</b>:7;
John <b>20</b>:27-28), not with knowledge or certainty. The emphasis falls on
the way we come to know something.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> There is some correlation between this
three-point format and the scientific method. Science has problem, hypothesis,
experimentation in the need, answer, and use positions. A good hypothesis has
predictability; so it explains even more than it was generated to explain. This
superadditum compares with honing and refining perceived need in the direction
of real need. There is a difference in that the &quot;answer&quot; in
Christianity comes to us from beyond us; we who are in need do not generate it.
Furthermore, revelation has authority beyond truthfulness, so we are then
doubly in no position to take part of it and leave or change the rest.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (7) <u>The purpose of Christian evidences</u>.
We maintained above that conversion contains no leaps, which means that the
evidence can connect unbelief with belief. An act of the will on that evidence
moves the person from one state to the next, decision being the only</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> <img
width=150 height=108 src="/cir-library/images/essays/part-i-overview-of-christian-apologetics/image002.png"></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>thing loosely comparable to a leap. No <u>objective
leap</u> inheres in the evidence itself. The leap is overcome by (a) previous
evidence, by (b) reciprocation between aspects of the process, and (c) by the
fact that a person can go back. So, apologetics can have an objective purposetracing
the process of entering into the circle of faith. Neither is there a <u>subjective
leap</u> in the personal conversion. Leap sounds like an emotional reaction
on the spur of the moment more than a decision, or a breakover. So the
purpose of apologetics is not limited to pointing out afterwards the continuity
a person could not appreciate before.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Not only are evangelism and conversion the
same process in identity and kind; conversion and growth are the same in kind. As
a result, the purpose of Christian evidences is to convict (John <b>10</b>:31
in A, C, D, <i>etc</i>.; Mark<b> 2</b>:10) and to confirm conviction (John <b>20</b>:31
in </span><span lang=HE dir=RTL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span dir=LTR></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'><span dir=LTR></span>*, B, <i>etc</i>.).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> The Spirit fits in our original diagram in
three ways as far as apologetics is concerned. (a) The Spirit operates through
general and special providence, preparing peoples sensitivity to their real
need. He does that indirectly through natural processes and through Christians that
proclaim and demonstrate the message. He does it through the message to
sensitize and convict. He may use miraculous manifestation to demonstrate Gods
real existence. (b) The Spirit is involved also in originating the message and
in bringing about the events that originated the message: Christs conception, the
Pentecostal empowerment, and so on. Finally, (c) he operates through sheer
presence to impact the believer.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;
margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:center'><b><span
style='font-size:14.0pt'>PART II: THE HISTORICAL METHOD </span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-right:-.5in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> I.  Analysis of Components Centered Around the
Historical Method</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  A.  Need</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The <b>first</b> given in peoples
experience is need conveyed by their dependent position in the world. The
feeling of need dependence generates has been styled <u>the sense of absolute
dependence</u>, or the sense of thrown-ness. It forces people to reflect on their
situation and to reach out for security amidst flux, safety amidst threat,
deliverance from limitation, and the like. Scripture declares that God withdrew
a more ideal circumstance from humanity evidently to force awareness of
dependence since as the withdrawal happened in association with disobedience. Limitations
bring mankind back to God, that is, to have apologetic force.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  A <b>second</b> given in human
nature is a <u>drive for meaningfulness</u>. Out of dependence comes a crisis
of meaning subjectively and objectively. Subjectively, meaninglessness is
suicidal. We do not ask why; it is just that way. If we become convinced that we
do not mean anything to somebody, we cannot bear to live. What ending life has
to do with being insignificant is unclear unless suicide assumes reason-to-be. Ecclesiastes
implies the necessity of meaningful living for wise peoples true happiness.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Objectively, dependence also
establishes a crisis of meaning for people. Dependent persons cannot purpose
for themselves and thus determine their own value; their purposes are always
subject to contravention by the higher reality. Only independent beings can
have independent meaning as well as decide the place and future of all else. Not
only do people have or not have a sense of worth, but it is intuitively obvious
that they are dependent and have purpose and worth relative to what is
sovereign. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  It is suicidal for people to be
driven for a level of meaning beyond what they have the ability to bring about.
There is a significant difference between what people may feel </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> <img
width=206 height=116 src="/cir-library/images/essays/part-i-overview-of-christian-apologetics/image003.png"></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>driven to have and the actual experience that they
receive from life. By virtue of a sovereign God who gives worth, Christianity
has the potential for bringing experience up to the drive level for meaning. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  A <b>third</b> given of humanness is
the <u>need for a sense of innocence</u>. Guilt is a destructive force in
people. As with meaninglessness, so also with conscious sinfulness: it is
suicidal. The importance of a clear conscience is illustrated by the
proliferation of ways for coping with it. Among them are mechanisms like <u>withdrawal</u>,
which puts distance between the offender and the knowing eyes of the offended. <u>Hardheartedness</u>
refuses to allow affective awareness of anything that is guilt-rendering. <u>Displacement</u>
seeks to convince oneself and others that responsibility does not rest on self.
<u>Deception</u> tries to cover up guilt so at least other people will not know
about it. <u>Self-punishment</u>, including suicide, consciously or
unconsciously attempts to balance the books by inflicting oneself with
deprivation, emotional stress, or even physical pain to achieve something like
self-salvation (autosoterism). <u>Rationalization</u> tries to define sin out
of existence. <u>Compensation</u>, as in penance or works, tries to make up for
absence of the good by doing more good than normal. Finally, Christs
answer comes as<u> forgiveness</u>. The fact of a past deed cannot be
eradicated, nor can it be denied its full character as sin; but it can be
forgiven. Thereafter it no longer affects present relationships, and life can
begin again; hence, it is called the </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>new birth.</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Repentance and apology serve as appropriate
prerequisites to guilt removal.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  A <b>fourth</b> given of human
nature is the <u>desire to be loved</u>. The ability to be loved is the best
point of contact with unbelievers. People may not be good at loving, but they
can appreciate being loved. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Alienation is the natural
consequence of wrongdoing, of self-centered behavior. Alienation brings
psychological pain. Even loneliness saps the vitality and radiance from
nearly any personality. The sense of acceptance in human relationships makes
noticeable changes in a persons demeanor and behavior. A better self-image
resulting from personal acceptance comes about because being loved gives a sense
of meaningfulness (1 Corinthians<b> 13</b>:1-3) and because meaning gets its
definition from relationship.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  For purposes of integration, it is
instructive to compare the treatment above with Maslows hierarchy of needs as
diagrammed below. The Christian message is clearly </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> <img width=355 height=211
src="/cir-library/images/essays/part-i-overview-of-christian-apologetics/image004.png"></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>relevant to the needs of modern man. The claim that
science replaces religion in the development of cultures may be true of some
religions, but science cannot deal with ultimate questions or satisfy peoples
psychological requirements. Even in our own culture, the age of materialistic
scientism seems to be disintegrating. Sense of dependence, drive for
meaningfulness, need for innocence, and desire for love inhere in the very
structure of humanness, and serve to sensitize the heart and mind to the
Christian answer for the human predicament.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  In summary, there are several
correlations between the provisions of Christianity and the concerns of man as
expressed by modern thinkers. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 
 Tillichs anxieties about:</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 1. Meaning Frankls will
to meaning  meaninglessness</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 2. Love Freuds
will to sex  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 3. Security will to
power  death</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Schleiermachers
<i>Abhngigkeit</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 4. Innocence 
 guilt</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 5. Freedom 
determinism</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>The perceived correlation between need and answer is
what we mean when we say of the Christian message it speaks to me, or it
preaches.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  B. Basis</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  1. History<span style='position:
relative;top:-3.0pt'>1</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  In chronological order, the
originating bases for the Christian faith lie prior to the events on which
Christianity rests. (1) The Christ event comes in the train of a long history
of <u>Gods dealings with the Jewish people</u>, among whom the Messiah arose (<b>prophecy</b>).
Jewish backgrounds relate to the Christ event as a special line of redemptive
history and through prophecy-fulfillment. Inasmuch as Jesus Messiah carries
forward that history and fulfills its anticipations, the evidential value
attached to that history accrues to Christianity as well.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Those operations of God among
the descendants of Abraham were authenticated by miracle. Similarly, (2) <u>various
aspects of the Christ event had their own authenticating marks</u>; so the
Messiahs coming can stand independently of the preceding history that enhances
it, culminating in the <b>empty-tomb/resurrection</b>. So Gentiles can find in
the good news an evidence not predicated on former considerations. Jewish
history and prophecy together with the ministry of John the Baptist, Jesus of
Nazareth, and his disciples form the positive grounding for Christianity. (For
a readable presentation of these matters, see Frank Morisons traditional
treatment in <i>Who Moved the Stone?</i> London: Faber and Faber, Ltd., 1930.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Time will tell has a
confirmatory role in validating the Messianic claims of Jesus and his
followers. (3) <u>The subsequent course of events in the Christian era</u>
tends to show that his original Jewish opponents erred about him (<b>test of
time</b>). That the faith has not perished from the earth does not prove it is
true; but if it had fallen away like other movements, it would be difficult to
believe in was true. Truth may not be the only thing that prevails, but
anything from God that is true must prevail.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Recognizing the historical
character of Christian evidences is most important in evaluating it. Part A in
the diagram of apologetics emphasizes the correlation between the gospel and human.
That test applies to all the worlds religions. but Christian evidence has a
second aspect somewhat independent of the first. By the fact that it depends on
historical events, Christian faith is subject to historical verification and
falsification beyond personal experience. Its truth is independent of recurrent
human experience. Besides its self-consistency and correlation with experience,
Christianitys historical base affords another class of evidence. That
three-dimensional foundation compounds the likelihood that it is true.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The person of Christ is the
most inclusive item in slot (2). We do not study historical events as such nor
do we study doctrine, ideas, morality as such. We introduce people in need to
the Person that can meet their need. We do well to use the expression Christ
event in this personalized sense.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Jesus himself staked the
validity of his ministry on his resurrection as the one great sign, which he
called the sign of Jonah because of its analogy to the episode in that Old
Testament prophets life (Matthew <b>12</b>:39; Luke <b>11</b>:29). Paul, the
apostle, staked the case for Christianity on the historicity of that same
event. </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>[&lt; </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>] means
to exalt, lift up, raise: <i>When you have lifted up the Son of man, then
you will know that I am and do nothing of myself</i> (John <b>8</b>:28). The
word surely refers to being lifted up in crucifixion rather than or to praise
or to exaltation at the right hand of the Father (Acts <b>5</b>:31). He means
the crucifixion that leads to the resurrection, and no one resurrects himself; so
all of Jesus previous ministry has the character of not being from himself like
resurrection does.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The following notes get at
significant features of Jeus resurrection from the dead. Christianity has a
unique relationship to history because its founding cluster of events originate
its message. Without Christ being who he was and doing what he did, there would
be no Christianity: it is a person-centered system. He was more than a prophet that
taught doctrines distinct to himself.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  a.  The empty tomb</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   (1) Basic points</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (a)  <u>Watch
of the soldiers</u> (Matthew<b> 27</b>:62-28:15). In anticipation of the
disciples attempt to remove the body from the grave and claim his
resurrection, the chief priests and Pharisees asked Pilate to authorize a guard
at the tomb until after the third day, which was when he said he would
resurrect.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (b)  <u>Large
stone across the door</u> (Matthew <b>27</b>:60; <b>28</b>:2; Mark <b>15</b>:46;
<b>16</b>:3-4; cp. John <b>20</b>:1). The stone was large enough that the women
who came that morning to finish burial preparations wondered how they could not
roll it away. Whether the Garden Tomb is the Lords burial place, it does indicate
the type of arrangement used to block the door from view and from scavengers (cp.
John<b> 11</b>:38-39). </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> in John <b>20</b>:1 has been taken to mean picked up
and moved from the tomb. But (1) the other accounts say </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>, and
(2) </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>can mean simply
to remove (1 Corinthians <b>5</b>:2, <i>e.g</i>.; note John <b>11</b>:39). It
is easier to adjust </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>to </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>than <i>vice
versa</i>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (c)  <u>Sealing
of the tomb</u> (Matthew <b>27</b>:66). Sealing does not mean plastering shut, but
affixing the mark of a seal on it to indicate any breach of governmental authority
in opening it (cp. Daniel <b>6:</b>16-18). It was much like that of the flimsy
little seals put on the doors of train cars and trucks that haul merchandise.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (d)  <u>Body
wrapped in linen</u> (Matthew <b>27</b>:59; Mark <b>15</b>:44; Luke <b>23</b>:53;
John <b>19</b>:40). This kind of burial cloth and its wrappings appear also in
the account of the resurrection of Lazarus (John <b>11</b>:45). Lazarus could
move enough to get out of the tomb. Depending on the condition of the body, it
would appear difficult to free oneself from inside the wrapping. The friends of
Lazarus assisted him.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (e)  <u>Bulk
of the burial spices</u> (John<b> 19</b>:39). It is sometimes said there would
be from fifty to one hundred pounds of these spices; that such was the case
with Lazarus is questionable, but the text says </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>
(John <b>19</b>:39): 100 Roman pounds, at 11.5 ounces apiece.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (f)  <u>Neat
(?) arrangement of the burial clothes</u> (John <b>20</b>:6-7). Twentieth-century
investigations of the relic identified traditionally as the burial shroud of
Jesus have revealed some interesting characteristics. The cloth, known as the
shroud of Turin, has received special attention in a number of books, including
Ian Wilsons <i>The Shroud of Turin: The Burial Cloth of Jesus?</i> (New York: Doubleday,
1978). These deflated grave clothes raise the question of where anyone would get
a used burial shroud except in a resurrection. (There are difficulties,
however, with identifying the shroud with the burial cloth of Jesus and other
explanations of it have been produced.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (2) Alternative
explanations</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (a) Jesus
was not dead (swoon theory).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  This
approach does not seem very convincing when we consider the condition of Jesus
body and other matters.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [1] <u>Even
before his crucifixion Jesus physical condition</u> was weakened from loss of
sleep, mental and emotional strain during the preceding days (Luke <b>22</b>:44),
the crown of thorns and the scourging by the Roman soldiers (Matthew <b>27</b>:26-30).
His condition explains conscripting Simon of Cyrene to bear his cross (John<b>
19</b>:17; Matthew <b>27</b>:32; Mark<b> 15</b>:21; Luke <b>23</b>:26). His
death so soon after the crucifixion (six hours) may indicate the same (John <b>19</b>:31-37;
Mark <b>15</b>:44).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [2]  The
<u>spear</u> <u>thrust</u> in his side by the soldier caused blood and water to
drain out of the wound (John <b>19</b>:34-35; cp. 1 John<b> 5</b>:6, 8?). If he
was not dead from the crucifixion, the spear thrust would have killed him since
the spear thrust was for making sure he was dead already. The blood and water
indicate either that the blood had begun to break down already or that the sack
around the heart was punctured by the spear point and drained. These soldiers
were sufficiently experienced in such matters to know when someone was dead, and
they were responsible for the execution.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [3] A
person in such deep <u>shock</u> like Jesus experienced is not revived by a
cool tomb. Successful medical treatment from shock requires keeping the body as
warm as possible.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [4] <u>Blood
poisoning</u> from the nails was commonly the ultimate cause of death in cases
where it was not hastened by breaking the leg bones.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   [5] In
light of his previous condition, had he lived through the scourging and other
maltreatment, the crucifixion itself, the <u>spear thrust</u>, the shock, and
the <u>blood poisoning</u>, he would hardly have been able, bundled in grave
clothes, to remove the <u>large stone</u> and elude the <u>group of soldiers</u>
who guarded the tomb (Matthew <b>27</b>:62-66). A better explanation would be
required.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (b) The body
was removed (Matthew<b> 27</b>:62-66; <b>28</b>:11-15).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Revived
in Hugh Schonfields <i>The Passover Plot: New Light on the History of Jesus</i>
(N.Y.: Bernard Geis Associates, 1966), the theory has had several forms. The
original one had the disciples stealing the body to claim their master had resurrected
(Matthew <b>27</b>:64). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Another
version has it that the gardener took the body elsewhere to save his garden
from being trampled (John <b>20</b>:15; Tertullian, <i>De Spectaculis</i> 30; <i>The
Gospel of Peter</i>; <i>The Book of the Resurrection</i>). Schonfields version
combines the idea with a plot Jesus arranged with secret disciples outside the
inner circle. They came to get the body to revive it. The trouble was that
Jesus had not counted on the spear thrust and so they could not revive him. Certain
considerations make these suggestions implausible as well.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [1] The
disciples did not expect him to resurrect. In contemporary Jewish thought, the
Messiah would <i>abide forever</i> (John <b>12</b>:36). By the very fact that
he could be killed, the leaders felt they had disproved his Messianic claims. Jesus
disciples shared this understanding about Messiah (Matthew <b>16</b>:21-16; <b>24</b>:20-21).
Had he been killed, the disciples would have become convinced that he was at
most a prophet. The gospel accounts show that this reaction was indeed their
response. Their frame of mind militates against having any inclination to steal
his body. His death would have disillusioned them, the fear of Roman reprisal
would have stayed their hand, and they would have gained nothing from it.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [2] What
reason could be given for leaving the napkin and </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> burial
cloth behind?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [3] Schonfields
rendition falters at this point as well, but more particularly in the person of
Jesus. We wonder what would cause someone who honestly thought he was Messiah
to make such an elaborate plot to survive, if need be, by deception, and later
to encourage another person to perpetuate the fraud. Given the presuppositions
Schonfield puts on Jesus, he surely would have known in his dying moments that
he was in fact <u>not</u> the Lords Messiah (p. 169; note pp. 176-80).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [4]  Later,
during the preaching of the resurrection, these men had their lives endangered,
they were beaten, and most were killed. Had their claims for Jesus resurrection
been false, they would surely not have died for a (1) known (2) falsehood that
was (3) contrary to their convictions.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [5]  From
an ethical standpoint we finds it difficult to believe that so high a moral
standard as the believers advocatedand demonstrated in many other particularswould
allow for perpetrating such a fraud.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [6]
The placement of a guard at the tomb decreases considerably the likelihood that
disciples would have tried to steal the corpse at all. On the next day after Preparation,
the guard was placed and the tomb was sealedpresumably on Saturday. After the
guard came, the disciples would not have carried out the plan even if they
could have overpowered the guards, because letting the theft be seen would
destroy the reason for stealing it. If the corpse had been removed before the
guard was set, the chief priests and Pharisees would have known it when they
sealed the stone.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  About
the only thing a disbeliever can do is to deny the truthfulness of the records
as a whole. In so doing, he selects what fits with his reconstruction and what
does not, automatically deleting anything supernatural.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [7]  That
the disciples stole the body while the soldiers were asleep does not fit; a
guard does not sleep. How would the guards know the <u>disciples stole</u> the
body if they were asleep?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [8] If
the disciples stole the body, why were they not arrested </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> and
prosecuted for it?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [9]  The
disciples kept themselves hidden behind locked doors, they so feared the Jews.
It is unlikely that such fear would steal a corpse.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   [10] The
disciples did not begin preaching the resurrection </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> right
away. Why, if they had stolen the body?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (c)  Mistaken
location of the tomb</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Kirsopp
Lake in <i>The Resurrection of Jesus Christ</i> gave </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> classical
expression to this theory.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [1] If
misidentification occurred, the scribes and Pharisees could have taken people
to the correct tomb and assured them that he had not arisen at all. They did
not follow this expediency.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [2] Joseph
of Arimathea (with Nicodemus) buried him in his own tomb (Matthew <b>27</b>:57-60;
cp. Mark<b> 15</b>:42-46; Luke <b>23</b>:50-54; John<b> 19</b>:38-42). The
women saw where the soldiers laid his body. Mary Magdalene and Mary the mother
of Joses/Joseph are singled out specifically (Matthew <b>27</b>:61; Mark <b>15</b>:47;
Luke <b>23</b>:55-56). Mary Magdalene and the other Mary were sitting nearby
watching (Matthew <b>27</b>:61), close enough to see <i>how the body was laid</i>
(Luke<b> 23</b>:55). Even if they had been mistaken on Sunday morning, the ones
that buried him would have known where they put himespecially Joseph, since it
was his own tomb. Other members of the Sanhedrin knew where to put the guards. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   [3]  Not
a great deal of confusion could have occurred since his tomb was right near
Golgotha (John <b>19</b>:41-42). It was a new tomb as well in a private garden
instead of a public cemetery. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [4]  Grave
clothes were left behind.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [5]  Soldiers
were at the tomb when an angel descended to </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> remove
the stone from the entrance.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-right:-.5in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  b.
 Appearances </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (1)
 List of appearances</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (a)
 Appearance to Mary (Mark <b>16</b>:9-11)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (b)
 Appearance to the three women (Matthew <b>28</b>:9-10)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (c)
 Appearance to the two disciples (Mark <b>16</b>:12-13; Luke<b> 24</b>:13-</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  22)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (d)
 Appearance to Peter (1 Corinthians <b>15</b>:5)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (e)
 Appearance to the ten (Mark <b>16</b>:14; Luke <b>24</b>:36-43; John </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> <b>20</b>:19-25)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (f)
 Appearance to the eleven (John <b>20</b>:26-31)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (g)
 Appearance to the seven (John <b>21</b>:1-23)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (h)
 Appearance to the five hundred (Matthew <b>28</b>:16-20; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  1
Corinthians <b>15</b>:6)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (i)
 Appearance in Jerusalem (Mark <b>16</b>:15-18)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (j)
 Appearance to James (1 Corinthians <b>15</b>:7)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (k)
 Appearance to the Twelve (Acts <b>1</b>:3-12; Mark<b> 16</b>:19-20; Luke </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> <b>24</b>:44-53) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (l)
 Appearance to Paul (Acts <b>9</b>,<b> 22</b>, <b>26</b>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (m)
 Appearance to Stephen (Acts <b>7</b>:55-56, subjective)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> (n)
 Vision of Christ (Revelation<b> 1</b>) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (2) Observations</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (a) These
were audible appearances in all cases where the</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  appearance
is described at length.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (b) He
ate with them (Luke<b> 24</b>:30?; John<b> 20</b>:17, 27), which</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  implies
that they were close to him.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (c) They
did not expect him to resurrect.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (d) They
were not gullible in believing reports of his resurrection.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [1] The
two on way to Emmaus (Luke <b>24</b>:17 + 21-24)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>   [2] Mary
supposed the gardener had taken the body (John </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> <b>20</b>:2,
13-15).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [3] The
women were going back to anoint the body.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> 
 [4] Thomas refused to believe at first (John<b> 20</b>:24-28).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> 
 [5] But some doubted (Matthew <b>28</b>:17; cp. John <b>9</b>:8-9)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [6] The
apostles did not believe Mary (Luke <b>24</b>:11; Mark </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> <b>16</b>:11).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (e) The
disciples were greatly afraid of the Jewish leaders.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (f) He
appeared, not just to one person, but to many at the same </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> time
(1 Corinthians <b>15</b>:6).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> (g) There
were some disbelievers who saw him afterwards: James, </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> the
soldiers, and Paul.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (h) Did
anyone see him arise? The soldiers?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>  [1]
more than one sense was involved,</span></p>
